  6. ORIGINAL REVIEW<br />After reading the great reviews and looking at the ingredients, I thought I had found a really great product to supplement my diet. I am a member of ConsumerLab.com. Consumer Lab is an independent laboratory that does analysis on all kinds of products. I trust them completely. Their analysis of Vibrant Health Green Vibrance revealed that each serving contains 24.3 mcg of arsenic. I don't know if that is a \\"safe\\" amount or not, but I personally don't want any amount of arsenic in my foods. I am sick to my stomach - literally - to find this out after using this product for over a month.<br /><br />EDIT<br />After doing more research I was disappointed to find out that ConsumerLab.com is not the trustworthy source I had first believed. In fact their report that Green Vibrance contains lead has been disputed as completely FALSE. The upside to this new discovery is that I can once again enjoy the benefits of Green Vibrance with complete confidence in their product. Anyone interested in more information on this subject can find it here on Amazon.com reviews.
  7. I have been taking Green Vibrance for only a few months, and thought I was doing my body a huge favor. Today (July 7, 2013) I got a report from ConsumerLab.com that states:<br /><br />\\"Vibrant Health Green Vibrance was found to contain 24.3 mcg of arsenic per scoop (12.1 grams). Further analysis showed that 5.4 mcg of this is \\"inorganic arsenic\\" reported to be the most toxic form of arsenic. Arsenic, like lead, is a heavy metal. The concern with inorganic arsenic is that it is a carcinogen (causing bladder, lung, and skin cancer and, potentially, liver, kidney, and prostate cancer) and can also have detrimental effects on organs and the circulatory system. Although there are no established federal limits for contaminants in supplements, in a liter of drinking water the EPA limits arsenic to 10 mcg of arsenic (which includes the inorganic plus the potentially less toxic organic form -- although the majority of arsenic in water is believed to [be] inorganic). No amount of arsenic is actually considered \\"safe\\" by the EPA. The EPA had considered a more stringent limit of 5 mcg of arsenic per liter, but concluded that 10 mcg provided a balance between safety and the cost of reducing arsenic levels. New Jersy adopted th more conservative 5 mcg limit. California, out of concern for the reproductive effects, has proposed that a product with more than 0.5 mcg of inorganic arsenic in a daily serving carry a warning label. As a carcinogen, California applies a limit of 10 mcg of inorganic arsenic per daily serving before a warning label is required.<br /><br />\\"In November 2012, Consumer Reports reported finding arsenic in many rice products, finding about 4 mcg of inorganic arsenic, on average, in a standard 45 gram (dry) serving of many types of rice sold in the U.X. Although this is only slightly less than the amount of inorganic arsenic in a serving of Green Vibrance, a scoop of Green Vibrance weighs only about 12 grams, meaning that the concentration of inorganic arsenicin Green Vibrance is around 5 times that in rice.   133. I saw this product in Whole Foods. I checked the nutritional profile, and was satisfied. I pay particular attention to the iron content: I steer clear away from anything with high iron content. The bottle in the store had an iron content of 3.95 mg. And, that was in the acceptable range (it's about 40% of RDA for a man or a menopausal woman. So, I ordered online. When I saw the nutritional profile again on the bottle that arrived, it had whopping 16.7 mg of iron, that's close to 170% of the RDA for a man or a menopausal woman. Note that high concentration of iron is not a GOOD thing at all: a lot of maladies are associated with this. The body does not have a natural way of getting rid of excess iron: only through blood donation or menstruation. So, if you are getting 170% of your daily RDA from this supplement, and then eat other food that contain iron (like, meat, beans, spinach, etc), you are accumulating a dangerous level of iron. I went back to the store to see whether I misread the nutritional table on the bottle sold in the store. Then I realized that there are several versions. The latest version, version 10.2 has a low iron content. Older version (version 10.1) is the one with incredibly high, almost dangerous level of iron. On the web site, they don't tell you which version they are selling, and they don't publish the nutritional profile. My guess is, they want to unload the older version with this major problem without really disclosing the details of their product. I will NOT buy any product of this company until they clearly show the nutritional profile of the product they are selling each time. This product is going to be returned PRONTO. Very deceptive selling process and hugely disappointing.

Now, I'm not a socialist and believe any business deserves to charge money for valuable services rendered. But they charge at BOTH ends... and that raised a few questions for me. Are they interested in educating the public, or are they just interested in making money?<br /><br />You might want to do further research before you claim 100% acceptance of this ConsumerLab report. Do a search for \\"Renaissance Health Publishing, LLC Warns the Public that ConsumerLab.com is Not Independent and Labels the 'CL Seal of Approval' a Worthless, Paid-For Advertising Gimmick.\\" There are a number of valid issues raised if you read the entire article. And if you dig deeper, with more searches, you'll find much more. This information ratcheted up my alarm level about their lab reports in general. While they appear to be doing good work, a healthy skepticism is in order.<br /><br />About arsenic in general:<br /><br />ALL natural greens and vegetables tend to higher in arsenic then we ideally would like. Being a natural product from the earth, the arsenic levels in fresh, living food can't be controlled in a laboratory. On the other hand, if you look at real people, and use common sense, consuming huge quantities of healthful greens seems to boost the immune system to a higher level so that energy, good health, and well-being can, and often does, last way into old age.<br /><br />IF there were a way to measure the life-time arsenic consumed by Jay Kordich (the original \\"Juice Man\\") or the now deceased Jack LaLanne (both passionate, life-long green juice/vegetable advocates) their levels would probably be higher than anyone could imagine, yet they achieved supremely good health. Kordich is now 90 years-old and LaLanne almost made it to 100 years-old. Both enjoy/ed amazing health, vigor, and energy far beyond many people half their age. The testimonies here by some elderly reviewers tend to reflect much the same.<br /><br />Parts of the US have higher arsenic soil levels where arsenic just occurs naturally. Other parts of the US have high levels due to farming practices. For example, in some parts of the cotton-growing South, arsenic-based pesticides were used to kill boll weevils on the cotton crops and arsenic levels are extremely high. Because arsenic dissolves easily in water, rice (which is grown in water) sucks up metals and arsenic and rice crops are a good indicator of soil health. Contrary to what most people think, most US rice is actually higher in arsenic than most Basmati and Jasmine rice grown in India or Thailand. Oddly enough, brown rice has higher concentrations of arsenic than white rice because arsenic is stored in the wheat germ which is removed during white rice processing!<br /><br />When I lived in southern California for a number of years, I was shocked to see how much heavy toxic chemical spraying goes on to grow the vegetables we buy in the market everywhere today. The Ag workers there don all manner of protective gear to work. Those vast fields are too toxic to walk in without serious protection and are barren of any life, with not an earthworm, bee, or butterfly to be seen for miles. Unless you can afford to buy strictly organic, the fresh produce you eat is usually bombarded with a constant chemical onslaught: pre-emergent soil herbicides, seed fungicides, pesticides, more fungicides for shipping, and often further chemicals to artificially ripen in the produce bin.<br /><br />As always, there are no simple answers in the supplement world. Unfortunately, we consumers must ask a lot of questions and do our own homework first.<br /><br />Good health and the human immune system are far more complex and mysterious than any stat from any chemical lab.<br /><br />Yes, arsenic consumed in higher levels is extremely poisonous and the effects are cumulative. That said, right now there's no serious research to show exactly what happens when we are exposed to low level, long-term arsenic consumption. In an ideal world, we would all grow, or buy, all our own food locally in tested, organically rich soil. But that is not going to happen any time soon.<br /><br />When I weigh the profound benefits of consuming life-giving raw vegetables and green supplements, arsenic is a very minor issue at this point.<br /><br />I WILL keep using this product. Meanwhile, I do hope someone from Vibrant Health Company addresses the arsenic report findings here ASAP for the benefit of all of us who consume this product.

There is little clinical study of many herbs, and reliable reporting on side effects (or even beneficial effects) is anecdotal. Herb popularity tends to run in fads -- there's always a hot new herb everyone is enthused about. And the excitement over the new one lasts about as long as it did with the last one. Still, because of the buzz, anything with herbs is considered by most people to be better than anything without herbs. Manufacturers get around the \\"what's hot\\" thing by throwing in the kitchen sink -- every herb that sounds good goes in the pot. Unfortunately that just increases the chances that some people are not going to be able to use the product. Or will use it and have reactions or side effects (or even long term effects) they don't realize are coming from an herb or herbs in the product. Green Vibrance happens to be one of those products with a kitchen sink full of herbs in addition to the green foods like spirulina and other beneficial ingredients. I didn't realize this when I took a serving. I had been looking forward to trying Green Vibrance because I had heard so much about it and read so many glowing reviews. A few hours later my blood sugar was way low -- I had the familiar and unmistakable symptoms. I was on schedule with my meals. The only thing I had done differently was try the Green Vibrance. I read the Green Vibrance label carefully and, among the many, many ingredients, discovered the likely culprit -- silymarin (milk thistle extract). I've had a similar experience with milk thistle before, as well as goldenseal. Do a Google search and you'll see silymarin has been noted as causing blood sugar drops. I really wish companies and corporations would get past the obsession with adding faddish herbs to every manufactured good out there. If we want herbs, we can easily buy them separately. Or the company could package and sell them as a separate adjunct to the product. For those who don't have blood sugar problems, Green Vibrance may be as wonderful as many people claim, but I'll just look for a green drink without all the added herb stuff.

Can't go wrong with that 4 page nutrition ingredient list! :) Cons: Allergies. Speaking of that 4 page ingredient list... I had a slight allergic reaction the first few times I took it. I'm rarely allergic to anything, but it's not that surprising that I did have slight flushing and itchiness considering the amount of unique ingredients in it, many of which I'm sure I've never ingested before. I slightly lowered my dosage and it doesn't do that anymore. Probiotics: The amounts of probiotics listed are \\"at date of manufacture\\" which does NOT necessarily mean \\"at date of ingestion\\". Refrigerate this product immediately to prevent any further loss of included probiotic cultures. Anticoagulant effects: You need to be aware of the many anti-inflammatory and anticoagulant ingredients in this product, as well as the one big coagulant. I remember reading one review of a man who got dangerously low blood pressure after taking this. He was taking Warfarin, a blood-thinning medication. I would NOT use this product if you take Warfarin. There are too many anti-inflammatory and anticoagulant ingredients that would enhance Warfarin, and possibly make your blood pressure dangerously low, AND there is 150% DV of Vitamin K in a normal dose, which very seriously conflicts with Warfarin as well as most all blood-thinners. If you aren't taking medication for blood pressure I wouldn't worry about it too much, though.
